The sewage treatment plant, which was originally built to provide municipal treatment services for Detroit in the early 1960s, was designed to treat Detroit's sewage through an environmentally safe process to prevent contamination and improve quality of life for residents of the nearby East Grand River Community. The rule states in pertinent part that an amendment to a general appropriation bill shall not be in order if changing existing law or if changing existing policy or procedure is in fact a change in the meaning or effect of existing law or that of existing policy or procedure.  The rule also makes it clear that a general appropriation bill shall not be amended to change existing law except where the change is clearly authorized by statute or other law.
